# Text Elements
Gaussian distribution ^iuKj9mtH

= mean ^gfI7NFyF

= Standard deviation ^VIetc5Jh

What is the standard deviation? ^OH2iNSrl

Standard deviation tells us how far apart
the elements are from each other by calculating all
the distances from their mean ^CNatNmtG

Remember that    is our Variance! ^DQ5aOx9I

2 ^SeEJZ7kT

What is the mean? ^VZFeDoTt

The mean is practically the "average" datapoint given
in our dataset such that all its features are averaged
"Center of mass" ^oPlqtnfh

The Gaussian distribution is a symmetric distribution of probabilities
centered around its mean and converges to zero the further away 
we go from the mean in either direction! ^VwDBha3S

Central limit theorem ^x084DeLi

We start with a random variable X
which is a randomized process that
each of its outcomes are associated
with a number ^uDTh399A

Under our 3 Critical assumptions
Add N samples of this variable
X1 + X2 + X3 + .... + XN ^N2d4helP

What does this mean? ^gnI5L4XL

How did we get to this equation?! ^aZIuwHYF

Why is it so ugly? ew! ^qKtXRMhI

What does PI have to do with it?? ^3TtJ6nwX

We can answer those
questions one by one

Lets start at the beginning ^btelUPRp

The distribution of this sum will look a lot like the Bell curve when N goes to Infinity ^pXI9x0s5

 = E[X] ^yszhITKq

Whats an expected value? ^VNMBCi9s

What is a variance? ^5u8uzYHG

Its the Expected value of the squared
distances of datapoints from the mean ^gTsWQpD3

Var = E[ (X-  ) ] ^kz7NR1HE

2 ^cQOxMECT

This doesnt really represent the distance
since its squared, but it is much nicer
to square the values than to use absolute values
due to requiring a positive distance for all points ^IEus0uqw

How do we calculate the variance of X+Y? ^6Ntck7Yk

weirdly enough, even though the variance does not represent
distances and the STD does, the variance is additive
which we are considering distribution X and Y

Var(X+Y) = Var(X) + Var(Y)


The STD actually does not spread out linearly, instead

STD(X1+X2+X3+...+XN) = STD(X1) * N ^j6XnZwg4

Assuming that X and Y are independent of each other ^3R4t4qRU

How do we derive this
equation from a
bell Curve? ^ycshXKYh

Firstly lets describe with the exponential function does ^u4qqGrsg

-x ^SJvZzEET

-|x| ^5cA4XT9P

= ^XcoO5ZUh

e ^f6zutK6C

-x ^4gbhO8Y4

2 ^puXbMLmA

Multiplying the exponential with a constant c will make our bell curve
Wider and narrower depending on the constant
Which also means that our base e is not special, its just chosen for readability ^XR1L7Qej

What if we divide x by our standard deviation and multiply by half?
Well then we can get out shape to deviate by sigma in each direction symmetrically ^JxefwHXJ

e ^G9tauOfh

2 ^0bUfG69y

1
2 ^tzyKmI6C

x
 ^UNg7iqyW

- ^INwIRNNM

Since this is a probability distribution function model we want
the area under the curve to be equal to 1
for reasons we wont get into, this curse actually has an area of sqrt(PI)
meaning if we divide by sqrt(PI) we can get this area to be 1 !
Keep in mind we also want to adjust the area under the curve to be 1 even when we
stretch it out using our deviation, thus we also want to divide by out "stretching" 
method which is  ^rOoeQnsV

We want to be able to shift our distribution
to the left and right according to its "center" 
which is exactly the mean of our distribution
this we put x-mean instead of x ^H9G8li5h

1
2    ^TmJdyfNq

* ^V0FZXl9K

1
 ^zurAXebr

* ^IHbtQE4h

e ^6mhREO0m

The standard normal distribution is when our mean is set to 0 and our deviation is set to 1
and the values that this function produces is how many deviations is our data far from the mean? ^VxU50PKG

WHAT ARE THOSE ASSUMPTIONS?? ^x2fe2Ym7

1. All Xi are independent events of each other!
2. All Xi are drawn from the same distribution!
3. the variance of our distributions is finite! ^wVDzigTP

Why the fuck is the area under the bell curve Sqrt(PI)? ^HSpYwxQg

Well its much more complicated than what I can explain here
but we can imagine our distribution as a symmetric hill in 3d
the area of our 2d normal distribution is just a small slice of it
the volume of the entire 3d distribution turns out to be PI from derivations 
and through integrals we figure out that our slice is actually
Square root of PI ^KSMk6iPv

Radially symmetric ^lto9RnQy

84062e6755da1c6bcf8f2ca5c67696d28d978a0c: $$\frac{1}{\sigma\sqrt{2\pi}}e^{-\frac{1}{2}(\frac{x-\mathcal{m}}{\sigma})^2}$$
